# pandas-datareader — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Next topic

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

On this page

pandas-datareader[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#pandas-datareader "Permalink to this headline")

=========================================================================================================================

Version: **0.10.0** Date: **July 13, 2021**

Up-to-date remote data access for pandas. Works for multiple versions of pandas.

Quick Start[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#quick-start "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Install using `pip`

pip install pandas-datareader

and then import and use one of the data readers. This example reads 5-years of 10-year constant maturity yields on U.S. government bonds.

import pandas\_datareader as pdr
pdr.get\_data\_fred('GS10')

Contents[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#contents "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Contents:

*   [Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html)
    
*   [Caching queries](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/cache.html)
    
*   [Other Data Sources](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html)
    
*   [Data Readers](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readers/index.html)
    
*   [What’s New](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html)
    

Documentation[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#documentation "Permalink to this headline")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Stable documentation](https://pydata.github.io/pandas-datareader/)
 is available on [github.io](https://pydata.github.io/pandas-datareader/)
. A second copy of the stable documentation is hosted on [read the docs](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/)
 for more details.

Recent developments[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#recent-developments "Permalink to this headline")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can install the latest development version using

pip install git+https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader.git

or

git clone https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader.git
cd pandas-datareader
python setup.py install

[Development documentation](https://pydata.github.io/pandas-datareader/devel/)
 is available for the latest changes in master.

Indices and tables[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/#indices-and-tables "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Index](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/genindex.html)
    
*   [Module Index](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/py-modindex.html)
    
*   [Search Page](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/search.html)
    

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html "next page")

=========================================================================================================================

Version: **0.10.0** Date: **July 13, 2021**

Up-to-date remote data access for pandas. Works for multiple versions of pandas.

# Caching queries — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Previous topic

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html "previous chapter")

#### Next topic

[Other Data Sources](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

Caching queries[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/cache.html#caching-queries "Permalink to this headline")

===============================================================================================================================

Making the same request repeatedly can use a lot of bandwidth, slow down your code and may result in your IP being banned.

`pandas-datareader` allows you to cache queries using `requests_cache` by passing a `requests_cache.Session` to `DataReader` or `Options` using the `session` parameter.

Below is an example with Yahoo! Finance. The session parameter is implemented for all datareaders.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: from pandas\_datareader.yahoo.headers import DEFAULT\_HEADERS

In \[3\]: import datetime

In \[4\]: import requests\_cache

In \[5\]: expire\_after \= datetime.timedelta(days\=3)

In \[6\]: session \= requests\_cache.CachedSession(cache\_name\='cache', backend\='sqlite', expire\_after\=expire\_after)

In \[7\]: session.headers \= DEFAULT\_HEADERS

In \[8\]: start \= datetime.datetime(2010, 1, 1)

In \[9\]: end \= datetime.datetime(2013, 1, 27)

In \[10\]: f \= web.DataReader("F", 'yahoo', start, end, session\=session)

In \[11\]: f.loc\['2010-01-04'\]
Out\[11\]: 
High         1.028000e+01
Low          1.005000e+01
Open         1.017000e+01
Close        1.028000e+01
Volume       6.085580e+07
Adj Close    6.968545e+00
Name: 2010-01-04 00:00:00, dtype: float64

A [SQLite](https://www.sqlite.org/)
 file named `cache.sqlite` will be created in the working directory, storing the request until the expiry date.

For additional information on using requests-cache, see the [documentation](https://requests-cache.readthedocs.io/)
.

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html "previous page")
 [Other Data Sources](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html "next page")

# Other Data Sources — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Previous topic

[Caching queries](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/cache.html "previous chapter")

#### Next topic

[Data Readers](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readers/index.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

On this page

Other Data Sources[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html#other-data-sources "Permalink to this headline")

========================================================================================================================================

Web interfaces are constantly evolving and so there is constant evolution in this space. There are a number of noteworthy Python packages that integrate into the PyData ecosystem that are more narrowly focused than pandas-datareader.

Alpha Vantage[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html#alpha-vantage "Permalink to this headline")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/)
 provides real time and historical equity data. Users are required to get a free API key before using the API. [Documentation](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 is available.

A [python package](https://github.com/RomelTorres/alpha_vantage)
 simplifying access is available on github.

Tiingo[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html#tiingo "Permalink to this headline")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tiingo](https://www.tiingo.com/)
 aims to make high-end financial tools accessible investors. The [API is documented](https://api.tiingo.com/)
. Users are required to get a free API key before using the API.

A [python package](https://github.com/hydrosquall/tiingo-python)
 simplifying access is available on github.

Barchart[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html#barchart "Permalink to this headline")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Barchart is a data provider covering a wide range of financial data. The [free API](https://www.barchart.com/ondemand/free-market-data-api)
 provides up to two years of historical data.

A [python package](https://github.com/femtotrader/barchart-ondemand-client-python)
 simplifying access is available on github.

List of Other Sources[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/see-also.html#list-of-other-sources "Permalink to this headline")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Awesome Quant](https://github.com/wilsonfreitas/awesome-quant#data-sources)
 maintains a large list of packages designed to provide access to financial data.

[Caching queries](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/cache.html "previous page")
 [Data Readers](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readers/index.html "next page")

---

# Remote Data Access — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Previous topic

[pandas-datareader](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/index.html "previous chapter")

#### Next topic

[Caching queries](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/cache.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

On this page

Remote Data Access[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-access "Permalink to this headline")

===========================================================================================================================================

Warning

The `access_key` keyword argument of `DataReader` has been deprecated in favor of `api_key`.

Functions from `pandas_datareader.data` and [`pandas_datareader.wb`](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readers/world-bank.html#module-pandas_datareader.wb "pandas_datareader.wb")
 extract data from various Internet sources into a pandas DataFrame. Currently the following sources are supported:

> *   [Tiingo](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-tiingo)
>     
> *   [IEX](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-iex)
>     
> *   [Alpha Vantage](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-alphavantage)
>     
> *   [Econdb](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-econdb)
>     
> *   [Enigma](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-enigma)
>     
> *   [Quandl](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-quandl)
>     
> *   [St.Louis FED (FRED)](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-fred)
>     
> *   [Kenneth French’s data library](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-ff)
>     
> *   [World Bank](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-wb)
>     
> *   [OECD](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-oecd)
>     
> *   [Eurostat](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-eurostat)
>     
> *   [Thrift Savings Plan](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-tsp)
>     
> *   [Nasdaq Trader symbol definitions](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-nasdaq-symbols)
>     
> *   [Stooq](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-stooq)
>     
> *   [MOEX](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-moex)
>     
> *   [Naver Finance](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-naver)
>     
> *   [Yahoo Finance](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#remote-data-yahoo)
>     

It should be noted, that various sources support different kinds of data, so not all sources implement the same methods and the data elements returned might also differ.

Tiingo[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#tiingo "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tiingo](https://www.tiingo.com/)
 is a tracing platform that provides a data api with historical end-of-day prices on equities, mutual funds and ETFs. Free registration is required to get an API key. Free accounts are rate limited and can access a limited number of symbols (500 at the time of writing).

In \[1\]: import os
In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader as pdr

In \[3\]: df \= pdr.get\_data\_tiingo('GOOG', api\_key\=os.getenv('TIINGO\_API\_KEY'))
In \[4\]: df.head()
                                close    high     low     open  volume  adjClose  adjHigh  adjLow  adjOpen  adjVolume  divCash  splitFactor
symbol date
GOOG   2014-03-27 00:00:00+00:00  558.46  568.00  552.92  568.000   13100    558.46   568.00  552.92  568.000      13100      0.0          1.0
       2014-03-28 00:00:00+00:00  559.99  566.43  558.67  561.200   41100    559.99   566.43  558.67  561.200      41100      0.0          1.0
       2014-03-31 00:00:00+00:00  556.97  567.00  556.93  566.890   10800    556.97   567.00  556.93  566.890      10800      0.0          1.0
       2014-04-01 00:00:00+00:00  567.16  568.45  558.71  558.710    7900    567.16   568.45  558.71  558.710       7900      0.0          1.0
       2014-04-02 00:00:00+00:00  567.00  604.83  562.19  565.106  146700    567.00   604.83  562.19  565.106     146700      0.0          1.0

IEX[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#iex "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Warning

Usage of all IEX readers now requires an API key. See below for additional information.

The Investors Exchange (IEX) provides a wide range of data through an [API](https://iexcloud.io/api/docs/)
. Historical stock prices are available for up to 15 years. The usage of these readers requires the publishable API key from IEX Cloud Console, which can be stored in the `IEX_API_KEY` environment variable.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: start \= datetime(2016, 9, 1)

In \[4\]: end \= datetime(2018, 9, 1)

In \[5\]: f \= web.DataReader('F', 'iex', start, end)

In \[6\]: f.loc\['2018-08-31'\]
Out\[6\]:
open             9.64
high             9.68
low              9.40
close            9.48
volume    76424884.00
Name: 2018-08-31, dtype: float64

Note

You must provide an API Key when using IEX. You can do this using `os.environ["IEX_API_KEY"] = "pk_xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"` or by exporting the key before starting the IPython session.

There are additional interfaces to this API that are directly exposed: tops (‘iex-tops’) and last (‘iex-lasts’). A third interface to the deep API is exposed through Deep class or the get\_iex\_book function.

import pandas\_datareader.data as web
f \= web.DataReader('gs', 'iex-tops')

Alpha Vantage[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#alpha-vantage "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides realtime equities and forex data. Free registration is required to get an API key.

### Historical Time Series Data[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#historical-time-series-data "Permalink to this headline")

Through the [Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 Time Series endpoints, it is possible to obtain historical equities and currency rate data for individual symbols. For daily, weekly, and monthly frequencies, 20+ years of historical data is available. The past 3-5 days of intraday data is also available.

The following endpoints are available:

*   `av-intraday` - Intraday Time Series
    
*   `av-daily` - Daily Time Series
    
*   `av-daily-adjusted` - Daily Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-weekly` - Weekly Time Series
    
*   `av-weekly-adjusted` - Weekly Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-monthly` - Monthly Time Series
    
*   `av-monthly-adjusted` - Monthly Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-forex-daily` - Daily Time Series
    

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[4\]: f \= web.DataReader("AAPL", "av-daily", start\=datetime(2017, 2, 9),
   ...:                   end\=datetime(2017, 5, 24),
   ...:                   api\_key\=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[5\]: f.loc\["2017-02-09"\]
Out\[5\]:
open      1.316500e+02
high      1.324450e+02
low       1.311200e+02
close     1.324200e+02
volume    2.834990e+07
Name: 2017-02-09, dtype: float64

To request the historical exchange rate of physical or digital currencies, use `av-forex-daily` and format the symbol as “FROM/TO”, for example “USD/JPY”.

The top-level function `get_data_alphavantage` is also provided. This function will return the `TIME_SERIES_DAILY` endpoint for the symbol and date range provided.

### Quotes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#quotes "Permalink to this headline")

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 Batch Stock Quotes endpoint allows the retrieval of realtime stock quotes for up to 100 symbols at once. These quotes are accessible through the top-level function `get_quote_av`.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[4\]: web.get\_quote\_av(\["AAPL", "TSLA"\])
Out\[4\]:
         price  volume            timestamp
symbol
AAPL    219.87     NaN  2019-09-16 15:59:59
TSLA    242.80     NaN  2019-09-16 15:59:57

Note

Most quotes are only available during market hours.

### Forex[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#forex "Permalink to this headline")

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides realtime currency exchange rates (for physical and digital currencies).

To request the exchange rate of physical or digital currencies, simply format as “FROM/TO” as in “USD/JPY”.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[3\]: f \= web.DataReader("USD/JPY", "av-forex",
    ...:                    api\_key=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: f
Out\[4\]:
                                 USD/JPY
From\_Currency Code                   USD
From\_Currency Name  United States Dollar
To\_Currency Code                     JPY
To\_Currency Name            Japanese Yen
Exchange Rate               108.17000000
Last Refreshed       2019-09-17 10:43:36
Time Zone                            UTC
Bid Price                   108.17000000
Ask Price                   108.17000000

Multiple pairs are are allowable:

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[3\]: f \= web.DataReader(\["USD/JPY", "BTC/CNY"\], "av-forex",
   ...:                   api\_key\=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: f
Out\[4\]:
                                 USD/JPY              BTC/CNY
From\_Currency Code                   USD                  BTC
From\_Currency Name  United States Dollar              Bitcoin
To\_Currency Code                     JPY                  CNY
To\_Currency Name            Japanese Yen         Chinese Yuan
Exchange Rate               108.17000000       72230.38039500
Last Refreshed       2019-09-17 10:44:35  2019-09-17 10:44:01
Time Zone                            UTC                  UTC
Bid Price                   108.17000000       72226.26407700
Ask Price                   108.17000000       72230.02554000

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides sector performances through the top-level function `get_sector_performance_av`.

Econdb[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#econdb "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Econdb](https://www.econdb.com/)
 provides economic data from 90+ official statistical agencies. Free API allows access to the complete Econdb database of time series aggregated into datasets.

Reading data for a single series such as the [RGDP](https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/)
 for United States, is as simple as taking the ticker segment from the URL path (`RGDPUS` in [https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/](https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/)
) and passing it in like:

import os
import pandas\_datareader.data as web

f \= web.DataReader('ticker=RGDPUS', 'econdb')
f.head()

The code snippet for exporting the whole dataset, or its filtered down subset, can be generated by using the Export -> Pandas Python3 functionality on any of the numerous datasets available, such as the Eurostat’s [GDP and main components](https://www.econdb.com/dataset/NAMQ_10_GDP)

import os
import pandas\_datareader.data as web

df \= web.DataReader('dataset=NAMQ\_10\_GDP&v=Geopolitical entity (reporting)&h=TIME&from=2018-05-01&to=2021-01-01&GEO=\[AL,AT,BE,BA,BG,HR,CY,CZ,DK,EE,EA19,FI,FR,DE,EL,HU,IS,IE,IT,XK,LV,LT,LU,MT,ME,NL,MK,NO,PL,PT,RO,RS,SK,SI,ES,SE,CH,TR,UK\]&NA\_ITEM=\[B1GQ\]&S\_ADJ=\[SCA\]&UNIT=\[CLV10\_MNAC\]', 'econdb')
df.columns

Datasets can be located through Econdb’s [search](https://www.econdb.com/search)
 engine, or discovered by exploring the [tree](https://www.econdb.com/tree/)
 of available statistical sources.

Enigma[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#enigma "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Access datasets from [Enigma](https://public.enigma.com/)
, the world’s largest repository of structured public data. Note that the Enigma URL has changed from [app.enigma.io](https://app.enigma.io/)
 as of release `0.6.0`, as the old API deprecated.

Datasets are unique identified by the `uuid4` at the end of a dataset’s web address. For example, the following code downloads from [USDA Food Recalls 1996 Data](https://public.enigma.com/datasets/292129b0-1275-44c8-a6a3-2a0881f24fe1)
.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader as pdr

In \[3\]: df \= pdr.get\_data\_enigma('292129b0-1275-44c8-a6a3-2a0881f24fe1', os.getenv('ENIGMA\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: df.columns
Out\[4\]:
Index(\['case\_number', 'recall\_notification\_report\_number',\
       'recall\_notification\_report\_url', 'date\_opened', 'date\_closed',\
       'recall\_class', 'press\_release', 'domestic\_est\_number', 'company\_name',\
       'imported\_product', 'foreign\_estab\_number', 'city', 'state', 'country',\
       'product', 'problem', 'description', 'total\_pounds\_recalled',\
       'pounds\_recovered'\],
      dtype='object')

Quandl[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#quandl "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Daily financial data (prices of stocks, ETFs etc.) from [Quandl](https://www.quandl.com/)
. The symbol names consist of two parts: DB name and symbol name. DB names can be all the [free ones listed on the Quandl website](https://blog.quandl.com/free-data-on-quandl)
. Symbol names vary with DB name; for WIKI (US stocks), they are the common ticker symbols, in some other cases (such as FSE) they can be a bit strange. Some sources are also mapped to suitable ISO country codes in the dot suffix style shown above, currently available for [BE, CN, DE, FR, IN, JP, NL, PT, UK, US](https://www.quandl.com/search?query=)
.

As of June 2017, each DB has a different data schema, the coverage in terms of time range is sometimes surprisingly small, and the data quality is not always good.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: symbol \= 'WIKI/AAPL'  \# or 'AAPL.US'

In \[3\]: df \= web.DataReader(symbol, 'quandl', '2015-01-01', '2015-01-05')

In \[4\]: df.loc\['2015-01-02'\]
Out\[4\]:
              Open    High     Low   Close      Volume  ...     AdjOpen     AdjHigh      AdjLow    AdjClose   AdjVolume
Date                                                    ...
2015-01-02  111.39  111.44  107.35  109.33  53204626.0  ...  105.820966  105.868466  101.982949  103.863957  53204626.0

World Bank[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#world-bank "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`pandas` users can easily access thousands of panel data series from the [World Bank’s World Development Indicators](http://data.worldbank.org/)
 by using the `wb` I/O functions.

### Indicators[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#indicators "Permalink to this headline")

Either from exploring the World Bank site, or using the search function included, every world bank indicator is accessible.

For example, if you wanted to compare the Gross Domestic Products per capita in constant dollars in North America, you would use the `search` function:

In \[1\]: from pandas\_datareader import wb
In \[2\]: matches \= wb.search('gdp.\*capita.\*const')

Then you would use the `download` function to acquire the data from the World Bank’s servers:

In \[3\]: dat \= wb.download(indicator\='NY.GDP.PCAP.KD', country\=\['US', 'CA', 'MX'\], start\=2005, end\=2008)

In \[4\]: print(dat)
                      NY.GDP.PCAP.KD
country       year
Canada        2008  36005.5004978584
              2007  36182.9138439757
              2006  35785.9698172849
              2005  35087.8925933298
Mexico        2008  8113.10219480083
              2007  8119.21298908649
              2006  7961.96818458178
              2005  7666.69796097264
United States 2008  43069.5819857208
              2007  43635.5852068142
              2006   43228.111147107
              2005  42516.3934699993

The resulting dataset is a properly formatted `DataFrame` with a hierarchical index, so it is easy to apply `.groupby` transformations to it:

In \[6\]: dat\['NY.GDP.PCAP.KD'\].groupby(level\=0).mean()
Out\[6\]:
country
Canada           35765.569188
Mexico            7965.245332
United States    43112.417952
dtype: float64

Now imagine you want to compare GDP to the share of people with cellphone contracts around the world.

In \[7\]: wb.search('cell.\*%').iloc\[:,:2\]
Out\[7\]:
                     id                                               name
3990  IT.CEL.SETS.FE.ZS  Mobile cellular telephone users, female (% of ...
3991  IT.CEL.SETS.MA.ZS  Mobile cellular telephone users, male (% of po...
4027      IT.MOB.COV.ZS  Population coverage of mobile cellular telepho...

Notice that this second search was much faster than the first one because `pandas` now has a cached list of available data series.

In \[13\]: ind \= \['NY.GDP.PCAP.KD', 'IT.MOB.COV.ZS'\]
In \[14\]: dat \= wb.download(indicator\=ind, country\='all', start\=2011, end\=2011).dropna()
In \[15\]: dat.columns \= \['gdp', 'cellphone'\]
In \[16\]: print(dat.tail())
                        gdp  cellphone
country   year
Swaziland 2011  2413.952853       94.9
Tunisia   2011  3687.340170      100.0
Uganda    2011   405.332501      100.0
Zambia    2011   767.911290       62.0
Zimbabwe  2011   419.236086       72.4

Finally, we use the `statsmodels` package to assess the relationship between our two variables using ordinary least squares regression. Unsurprisingly, populations in rich countries tend to use cellphones at a higher rate:

In \[17\]: import numpy as np
In \[18\]: import statsmodels.formula.api as smf
In \[19\]: mod \= smf.ols('cellphone ~ np.log(gdp)', dat).fit()
In \[20\]: print(mod.summary())
                            OLS Regression Results

Method:                 Least Squares   F\-statistic:                     13.08
Date:                Thu, 25 Jul 2013   Prob (F\-statistic):            0.00105
Time:                        15:24:42   Log\-Likelihood:                \-139.16

\-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Country Codes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#country-codes "Permalink to this headline")

The `country` argument accepts a string or list of mixed [two](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2)
 or [three](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3)
 character ISO country codes, as well as dynamic [World Bank exceptions](https://datahelpdesk.worldbank.org/knowledgebase/articles/898590-api-country-queries)
 to the ISO standards.

For a list of the the hard-coded country codes (used solely for error handling logic) see `pandas_datareader.wb.country_codes`.

### Problematic Country Codes & Indicators[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#problematic-country-codes-indicators "Permalink to this headline")

Note

The World Bank’s country list and indicators are dynamic. As of 0.15.1, [`wb.download()`](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/readers/world-bank.html#pandas_datareader.wb.download "pandas_datareader.wb.download")
 is more flexible. To achieve this, the warning and exception logic changed.

The world bank converts some country codes, in their response, which makes error checking by pandas difficult. Retired indicators still persist in the search.

Given the new flexibility of 0.15.1, improved error handling by the user may be necessary for fringe cases.

To help identify issues:

There are at least 4 kinds of country codes:

1.  Standard (2/3 digit ISO) - returns data, will warn and error properly.
    
2.  Non-standard (WB Exceptions) - returns data, but will falsely warn.
    
3.  Blank - silently missing from the response.
    
4.  Bad - causes the entire response from WB to fail, always exception inducing.
    

There are at least 3 kinds of indicators:

1.  Current - Returns data.
    
2.  Retired - Appears in search results, yet won’t return data.
    
3.  Bad - Will not return data.
    

Use the `errors` argument to control warnings and exceptions. Setting errors to ignore or warn, won’t stop failed responses. (ie, 100% bad indicators, or a single ‘bad’ (#4 above) country code).

See docstrings for more info.

OECD[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#oecd "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[OECD Statistics](http://stats.oecd.org/)
 are available via `DataReader`. You have to specify OECD’s data set code.

To confirm data set code, access to `each data -> Export -> SDMX Query`. Following example is to download ‘Trade Union Density’ data which set code is ‘TUD’.

Eurostat[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#eurostat "Permalink to this headline")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Eurostat](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/)
 are available via `DataReader`.

Get [Rail accidents by type of accident (ERA data)](http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran_sf_railac&lang=en)
 data. The result will be a `DataFrame` which has `DatetimeIndex` as index and `MultiIndex` of attributes or countries as column. The target URL is:

*   [http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran\_sf\_railac&lang=en](http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran_sf_railac&lang=en)
    

You can specify dataset ID ‘tran\_sf\_railac’ to get corresponding data via `DataReader`.

In \[20\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[21\]: df \= web.DataReader('tran\_sf\_railac', 'eurostat')

In \[22\]: df
Out\[22\]:

Yahoo Finance Data[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/remote_data.html#yahoo-finance-data "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Yahoo Finance provides stock market data

The following endpoints are available:

*   `yahoo` - retrieve daily stock prices (high, open, close, volu,e and adjusted close)
    
*   `yahoo-actions` - retrieve historical corporate actions (dividends and stock splits)
    
*   `yahoo-dividends` - retrieve historical dividends
    

In \[39\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[40\]: import pandas as pd

In \[41\]: import datetime as dt

In \[42\]: df \= web.DataReader('GE', 'yahoo', start\='2019-09-10', end\='2019-10-09')

# Caching queries — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Previous topic

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html "previous chapter")

#### Next topic

[Other Data Sources](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/see-also.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

Caching queries[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/cache.html#caching-queries "Permalink to this headline")

===============================================================================================================================

Making the same request repeatedly can use a lot of bandwidth, slow down your code and may result in your IP being banned.

`pandas-datareader` allows you to cache queries using `requests_cache` by passing a `requests_cache.Session` to `DataReader` or `Options` using the `session` parameter.

Below is an example with Yahoo! Finance. The session parameter is implemented for all datareaders.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: from pandas\_datareader.yahoo.headers import DEFAULT\_HEADERS

In \[3\]: import datetime

In \[4\]: import requests\_cache

In \[5\]: expire\_after \= datetime.timedelta(days\=3)

In \[6\]: session \= requests\_cache.CachedSession(cache\_name\='cache', backend\='sqlite', expire\_after\=expire\_after)

In \[7\]: session.headers \= DEFAULT\_HEADERS

In \[8\]: start \= datetime.datetime(2010, 1, 1)

In \[9\]: end \= datetime.datetime(2013, 1, 27)

In \[10\]: f \= web.DataReader("F", 'yahoo', start, end, session\=session)

In \[11\]: f.loc\['2010-01-04'\]
Out\[11\]: 
High         1.028000e+01
Low          1.005000e+01
Open         1.017000e+01
Close        1.028000e+01
Volume       6.085580e+07
Adj Close    6.968545e+00
Name: 2010-01-04 00:00:00, dtype: float64

A [SQLite](https://www.sqlite.org/)
 file named `cache.sqlite` will be created in the working directory, storing the request until the expiry date.

For additional information on using requests-cache, see the [documentation](https://requests-cache.readthedocs.io/)
.

[Remote Data Access](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html "previous page")
 [Other Data Sources](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/see-also.html "next page")

# Remote Data Access — pandas-datareader 0.10.0 documentation

#### Previous topic

[pandas-datareader](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/index.html "previous chapter")

#### Next topic

[Caching queries](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/cache.html "next chapter")

### Quick search

   

On this page

Remote Data Access[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-access "Permalink to this headline")

===========================================================================================================================================

Warning

The `access_key` keyword argument of `DataReader` has been deprecated in favor of `api_key`.

Functions from `pandas_datareader.data` and [`pandas_datareader.wb`](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/readers/world-bank.html#module-pandas_datareader.wb "pandas_datareader.wb")
 extract data from various Internet sources into a pandas DataFrame. Currently the following sources are supported:

> *   [Tiingo](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-tiingo)
>     
> *   [IEX](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-iex)
>     
> *   [Alpha Vantage](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-alphavantage)
>     
> *   [Econdb](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-econdb)
>     
> *   [Enigma](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-enigma)
>     
> *   [Quandl](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-quandl)
>     
> *   [St.Louis FED (FRED)](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-fred)
>     
> *   [Kenneth French’s data library](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-ff)
>     
> *   [World Bank](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-wb)
>     
> *   [OECD](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-oecd)
>     
> *   [Eurostat](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-eurostat)
>     
> *   [Thrift Savings Plan](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-tsp)
>     
> *   [Nasdaq Trader symbol definitions](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-nasdaq-symbols)
>     
> *   [Stooq](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-stooq)
>     
> *   [MOEX](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-moex)
>     
> *   [Naver Finance](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-naver)
>     
> *   [Yahoo Finance](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#remote-data-yahoo)
>     

It should be noted, that various sources support different kinds of data, so not all sources implement the same methods and the data elements returned might also differ.

Tiingo[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#tiingo "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Tiingo](https://www.tiingo.com/)
 is a tracing platform that provides a data api with historical end-of-day prices on equities, mutual funds and ETFs. Free registration is required to get an API key. Free accounts are rate limited and can access a limited number of symbols (500 at the time of writing).

In \[1\]: import os
In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader as pdr

In \[3\]: df \= pdr.get\_data\_tiingo('GOOG', api\_key\=os.getenv('TIINGO\_API\_KEY'))
In \[4\]: df.head()
                                close    high     low     open  volume  adjClose  adjHigh  adjLow  adjOpen  adjVolume  divCash  splitFactor

       2014-03-28 00:00:00+00:00  559.99  566.43  558.67  561.200   41100    559.99   566.43  558.67  561.200      41100      0.0          1.0
       2014-03-31 00:00:00+00:00  556.97  567.00  556.93  566.890   10800    556.97   567.00  556.93  566.890      10800      0.0          1.0
       2014-04-01 00:00:00+00:00  567.16  568.45  558.71  558.710    7900    567.16   568.45  558.71  558.710       7900      0.0          1.0
       2014-04-02 00:00:00+00:00  567.00  604.83  562.19  565.106  146700    567.00   604.83  562.19  565.106     146700      0.0          1.0

IEX[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#iex "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Warning

Usage of all IEX readers now requires an API key. See below for additional information.

The Investors Exchange (IEX) provides a wide range of data through an [API](https://iexcloud.io/api/docs/)
. Historical stock prices are available for up to 15 years. The usage of these readers requires the publishable API key from IEX Cloud Console, which can be stored in the `IEX_API_KEY` environment variable.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: start \= datetime(2016, 9, 1)

In \[4\]: end \= datetime(2018, 9, 1)

In \[5\]: f \= web.DataReader('F', 'iex', start, end)

In \[6\]: f.loc\['2018-08-31'\]
Out\[6\]:
open             9.64
high             9.68
low              9.40
close            9.48
volume    76424884.00
Name: 2018-08-31, dtype: float64

Note

You must provide an API Key when using IEX. You can do this using `os.environ["IEX_API_KEY"] = "pk_xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx"` or by exporting the key before starting the IPython session.

There are additional interfaces to this API that are directly exposed: tops (‘iex-tops’) and last (‘iex-lasts’). A third interface to the deep API is exposed through Deep class or the get\_iex\_book function.

Execute block when markets are open

import pandas\_datareader.data as web
f \= web.DataReader('gs', 'iex-tops')
f\[:10\]

Alpha Vantage[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#alpha-vantage "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides realtime equities and forex data. Free registration is required to get an API key.

### Historical Time Series Data[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#historical-time-series-data "Permalink to this headline")

Through the [Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 Time Series endpoints, it is possible to obtain historical equities and currency rate data for individual symbols. For daily, weekly, and monthly frequencies, 20+ years of historical data is available. The past 3-5 days of intraday data is also available.

The following endpoints are available:

*   `av-intraday` - Intraday Time Series
    
*   `av-daily` - Daily Time Series
    
*   `av-daily-adjusted` - Daily Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-weekly` - Weekly Time Series
    
*   `av-weekly-adjusted` - Weekly Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-monthly` - Monthly Time Series
    
*   `av-monthly-adjusted` - Monthly Time Series (Adjusted)
    
*   `av-forex-daily` - Daily Time Series
    

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[4\]: f \= web.DataReader("AAPL", "av-daily", start\=datetime(2017, 2, 9),
   ...:                   end\=datetime(2017, 5, 24),
   ...:                   api\_key\=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[5\]: f.loc\["2017-02-09"\]
Out\[5\]:
open      1.316500e+02
high      1.324450e+02
low       1.311200e+02
close     1.324200e+02
volume    2.834990e+07
Name: 2017-02-09, dtype: float64

To request the historical exchange rate of physical or digital currencies, use `av-forex-daily` and format the symbol as “FROM/TO”, for example “USD/JPY”.

The top-level function `get_data_alphavantage` is also provided. This function will return the `TIME_SERIES_DAILY` endpoint for the symbol and date range provided.

### Quotes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#quotes "Permalink to this headline")

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 Batch Stock Quotes endpoint allows the retrieval of realtime stock quotes for up to 100 symbols at once. These quotes are accessible through the top-level function `get_quote_av`.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: from datetime import datetime

In \[3\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[4\]: web.get\_quote\_av(\["AAPL", "TSLA"\])
Out\[4\]:
         price  volume            timestamp
symbol
AAPL    219.87     NaN  2019-09-16 15:59:59
TSLA    242.80     NaN  2019-09-16 15:59:57

Note

Most quotes are only available during market hours.

### Forex[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#forex "Permalink to this headline")

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides realtime currency exchange rates (for physical and digital currencies).

To request the exchange rate of physical or digital currencies, simply format as “FROM/TO” as in “USD/JPY”.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[3\]: f \= web.DataReader("USD/JPY", "av-forex",
    ...:                    api\_key=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: f
Out\[4\]:
                                 USD/JPY

To\_Currency Name            Japanese Yen
Exchange Rate               108.17000000
Last Refreshed       2019-09-17 10:43:36
Time Zone                            UTC
Bid Price                   108.17000000
Ask Price                   108.17000000

Multiple pairs are are allowable:

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[3\]: f \= web.DataReader(\["USD/JPY", "BTC/CNY"\], "av-forex",
   ...:                   api\_key\=os.getenv('ALPHAVANTAGE\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: f
Out\[4\]:

Ask Price                   108.17000000       72230.02554000

### Sector Performance[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#sector-performance "Permalink to this headline")

[Alpha Vantage](https://www.alphavantage.co/documentation)
 provides sector performances through the top-level function `get_sector_performance_av`.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[3\]: web.get\_sector\_performance\_av().head()
Out\[4\]:
                 RT      1D      5D      1M     3M     YTD       1Y      3Y       5Y      10Y
Energy        3.29%   3.29%   4.82%  11.69%  3.37%   9.07%  -15.26%  -7.69%  -32.31%   12.15%

Econdb[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#econdb "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Econdb](https://www.econdb.com/)
 provides economic data from 90+ official statistical agencies. Free API allows access to the complete Econdb database of time series aggregated into datasets.

Reading data for a single series such as the [RGDP](https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/)
 for United States, is as simple as taking the ticker segment from the URL path (`RGDPUS` in [https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/](https://www.econdb.com/series/RGDPUS/)
) and passing it in like:

import os
import pandas\_datareader.data as web

f \= web.DataReader('ticker=RGDPUS', 'econdb')
f.head()

The code snippet for exporting the whole dataset, or its filtered down subset, can be generated by using the Export -> Pandas Python3 functionality on any of the numerous datasets available, such as the Eurostat’s [GDP and main components](https://www.econdb.com/dataset/NAMQ_10_GDP)

import os
import pandas\_datareader.data as web

df \= web.DataReader('dataset=NAMQ\_10\_GDP&v=Geopolitical entity (reporting)&h=TIME&from=2018-05-01&to=2021-01-01&GEO=\[AL,AT,BE,BA,BG,HR,CY,CZ,DK,EE,EA19,FI,FR,DE,EL,HU,IS,IE,IT,XK,LV,LT,LU,MT,ME,NL,MK,NO,PL,PT,RO,RS,SK,SI,ES,SE,CH,TR,UK\]&NA\_ITEM=\[B1GQ\]&S\_ADJ=\[SCA\]&UNIT=\[CLV10\_MNAC\]', 'econdb')
df.columns

Datasets can be located through Econdb’s [search](https://www.econdb.com/search)
 engine, or discovered by exploring the [tree](https://www.econdb.com/tree/)
 of available statistical sources.

Enigma[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#enigma "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Access datasets from [Enigma](https://public.enigma.com/)
, the world’s largest repository of structured public data. Note that the Enigma URL has changed from [app.enigma.io](https://app.enigma.io/)
 as of release `0.6.0`, as the old API deprecated.

Datasets are unique identified by the `uuid4` at the end of a dataset’s web address. For example, the following code downloads from [USDA Food Recalls 1996 Data](https://public.enigma.com/datasets/292129b0-1275-44c8-a6a3-2a0881f24fe1)
.

In \[1\]: import os

In \[2\]: import pandas\_datareader as pdr

In \[3\]: df \= pdr.get\_data\_enigma('292129b0-1275-44c8-a6a3-2a0881f24fe1', os.getenv('ENIGMA\_API\_KEY'))

In \[4\]: df.columns
Out\[4\]:
Index(\['case\_number', 'recall\_notification\_report\_number',\
       'recall\_notification\_report\_url', 'date\_opened', 'date\_closed',\
       'recall\_class', 'press\_release', 'domestic\_est\_number', 'company\_name',\
       'imported\_product', 'foreign\_estab\_number', 'city', 'state', 'country',\
       'product', 'problem', 'description', 'total\_pounds\_recalled',\
       'pounds\_recovered'\],
      dtype='object')

Quandl[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#quandl "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Daily financial data (prices of stocks, ETFs etc.) from [Quandl](https://www.quandl.com/)
. The symbol names consist of two parts: DB name and symbol name. DB names can be all the [free ones listed on the Quandl website](https://blog.quandl.com/free-data-on-quandl)
. Symbol names vary with DB name; for WIKI (US stocks), they are the common ticker symbols, in some other cases (such as FSE) they can be a bit strange. Some sources are also mapped to suitable ISO country codes in the dot suffix style shown above, currently available for [BE, CN, DE, FR, IN, JP, NL, PT, UK, US](https://www.quandl.com/search?query=)
.

As of June 2017, each DB has a different data schema, the coverage in terms of time range is sometimes surprisingly small, and the data quality is not always good.

In \[1\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[2\]: symbol \= 'WIKI/AAPL'  \# or 'AAPL.US'

In \[3\]: df \= web.DataReader(symbol, 'quandl', '2015-01-01', '2015-01-05')

In \[4\]: df.loc\['2015-01-02'\]
Out\[4\]:
              Open    High     Low   Close      Volume  ...     AdjOpen     AdjHigh      AdjLow    AdjClose   AdjVolume
Date                                                    ...
2015-01-02  111.39  111.44  107.35  109.33  53204626.0  ...  105.820966  105.868466  101.982949  103.863957  53204626.0

World Bank[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#world-bank "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`pandas` users can easily access thousands of panel data series from the [World Bank’s World Development Indicators](http://data.worldbank.org/)
 by using the `wb` I/O functions.

### Indicators[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#indicators "Permalink to this headline")

Either from exploring the World Bank site, or using the search function included, every world bank indicator is accessible.

For example, if you wanted to compare the Gross Domestic Products per capita in constant dollars in North America, you would use the `search` function:

In \[1\]: from pandas\_datareader import wb
In \[2\]: matches \= wb.search('gdp.\*capita.\*const')

Then you would use the `download` function to acquire the data from the World Bank’s servers:

In \[3\]: dat \= wb.download(indicator\='NY.GDP.PCAP.KD', country\=\['US', 'CA', 'MX'\], start\=2005, end\=2008)

In \[4\]: print(dat)
                      NY.GDP.PCAP.KD
country       year
Canada        2008  36005.5004978584
              2007  36182.9138439757
              2006  35785.9698172849
              2005  35087.8925933298
Mexico        2008  8113.10219480083
              2007  8119.21298908649
              2006  7961.96818458178
              2005  7666.69796097264
United States 2008  43069.5819857208
              2007  43635.5852068142
              2006   43228.111147107
              2005  42516.3934699993

The resulting dataset is a properly formatted `DataFrame` with a hierarchical index, so it is easy to apply `.groupby` transformations to it:

In \[6\]: dat\['NY.GDP.PCAP.KD'\].groupby(level\=0).mean()
Out\[6\]:
country
Canada           35765.569188
Mexico            7965.245332
United States    43112.417952
dtype: float64

Now imagine you want to compare GDP to the share of people with cellphone contracts around the world.

In \[7\]: wb.search('cell.\*%').iloc\[:,:2\]
Out\[7\]:
                     id                                               name
3990  IT.CEL.SETS.FE.ZS  Mobile cellular telephone users, female (% of ...
3991  IT.CEL.SETS.MA.ZS  Mobile cellular telephone users, male (% of po...
4027      IT.MOB.COV.ZS  Population coverage of mobile cellular telepho...

Notice that this second search was much faster than the first one because `pandas` now has a cached list of available data series.

In \[13\]: ind \= \['NY.GDP.PCAP.KD', 'IT.MOB.COV.ZS'\]
In \[14\]: dat \= wb.download(indicator\=ind, country\='all', start\=2011, end\=2011).dropna()
In \[15\]: dat.columns \= \['gdp', 'cellphone'\]
In \[16\]: print(dat.tail())
                        gdp  cellphone
country   year
Swaziland 2011  2413.952853       94.9
Tunisia   2011  3687.340170      100.0
Uganda    2011   405.332501      100.0
Zambia    2011   767.911290       62.0
Zimbabwe  2011   419.236086       72.4

Finally, we use the `statsmodels` package to assess the relationship between our two variables using ordinary least squares regression. Unsurprisingly, populations in rich countries tend to use cellphones at a higher rate:

In \[17\]: import numpy as np
In \[18\]: import statsmodels.formula.api as smf
In \[19\]: mod \= smf.ols('cellphone ~ np.log(gdp)', dat).fit()
In \[20\]: print(mod.summary())
                            OLS Regression Results

### Country Codes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#country-codes "Permalink to this headline")

The `country` argument accepts a string or list of mixed [two](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2)
 or [three](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3)
 character ISO country codes, as well as dynamic [World Bank exceptions](https://datahelpdesk.worldbank.org/knowledgebase/articles/898590-api-country-queries)
 to the ISO standards.

For a list of the the hard-coded country codes (used solely for error handling logic) see `pandas_datareader.wb.country_codes`.

### Problematic Country Codes & Indicators[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#problematic-country-codes-indicators "Permalink to this headline")

Note

The World Bank’s country list and indicators are dynamic. As of 0.15.1, [`wb.download()`](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/readers/world-bank.html#pandas_datareader.wb.download "pandas_datareader.wb.download")
 is more flexible. To achieve this, the warning and exception logic changed.

The world bank converts some country codes, in their response, which makes error checking by pandas difficult. Retired indicators still persist in the search.

Given the new flexibility of 0.15.1, improved error handling by the user may be necessary for fringe cases.

To help identify issues:

There are at least 4 kinds of country codes:

1.  Standard (2/3 digit ISO) - returns data, will warn and error properly.
    
2.  Non-standard (WB Exceptions) - returns data, but will falsely warn.
    
3.  Blank - silently missing from the response.
    
4.  Bad - causes the entire response from WB to fail, always exception inducing.
    

There are at least 3 kinds of indicators:

1.  Current - Returns data.
    
2.  Retired - Appears in search results, yet won’t return data.
    
3.  Bad - Will not return data.
    

Use the `errors` argument to control warnings and exceptions. Setting errors to ignore or warn, won’t stop failed responses. (ie, 100% bad indicators, or a single ‘bad’ (#4 above) country code).

See docstrings for more info.

OECD[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#oecd "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[OECD Statistics](http://stats.oecd.org/)
 are available via `DataReader`. You have to specify OECD’s data set code.

To confirm data set code, access to `each data -> Export -> SDMX Query`. Following example is to download ‘Trade Union Density’ data which set code is ‘TUD’.

In \[15\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[16\]: import datetime

In \[17\]: df \= web.DataReader('TUD', 'oecd')

Eurostat[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#eurostat "Permalink to this headline")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Eurostat](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/)
 are available via `DataReader`.

Get [Rail accidents by type of accident (ERA data)](http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran_sf_railac&lang=en)
 data. The result will be a `DataFrame` which has `DatetimeIndex` as index and `MultiIndex` of attributes or countries as column. The target URL is:

*   [http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran\_sf\_railac&lang=en](http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=tran_sf_railac&lang=en)
    

You can specify dataset ID ‘tran\_sf\_railac’ to get corresponding data via `DataReader`.

Naver Finance Data[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#naver-finance-data "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Naver Finance](https://finance.naver.com/)
 provides Korean stock market ([KOSPI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KOSPI)
, [KOSDAQ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KOSDAQ)
) historical data.

Yahoo Finance Data[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/stable/remote_data.html#yahoo-finance-data "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Yahoo Finance provides stock market data

The following endpoints are available:

*   `yahoo` - retrieve daily stock prices (high, open, close, volu,e and adjusted close)
    
*   `yahoo-actions` - retrieve historical corporate actions (dividends and stock splits)
    
*   `yahoo-dividends` - retrieve historical dividends
    

In \[39\]: import pandas\_datareader.data as web

In \[40\]: import pandas as pd

In \[41\]: import datetime as dt

In \[42\]: df \= web.DataReader('GE', 'yahoo', start\='2019-09-10', end\='2019-10-09')

In \[43\]: df.head()
Out\[43\]: 
            High   Low  Open  Close      Volume  Adj Close
Date                                                      
2019-09-10  9.27  8.90  8.91   9.14  62617200.0   9.062220
2019-09-11  9.36  9.06  9.15   9.36  57094900.0   9.280347
2019-09-12  9.52  9.22  9.40   9.26  68115100.0   9.181198
2019-09-13  9.45  9.14  9.31   9.34  45589400.0   9.270529
2019-09-16  9.42  9.17  9.30   9.38  45748400.0   9.310231

In \[44\]: start \= dt.datetime(2010, 1, 29)

In \[45\]: end \= dt.datetime.today()

In \[46\]: actions \= web.DataReader('GOOG', 'yahoo-actions', start, end)

In \[47\]: actions.head()
Out\[47\]: 
           action     value
2015-04-27  SPLIT  0.997262
2014-03-27  SPLIT  0.499500

In \[48\]: dividends \= web.DataReader('IBM', 'yahoo-dividends', start, end)

v0.9.0 (July 10, 2020)[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#v0-9-0-july-10-2020 "Permalink to this headline")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Highlights include:

What’s new in v0.9.0

*   [Enhancements](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-090-enhancements)
    
*   [Backwards incompatible API changes](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#backwards-incompatible-api-changes)
    
*   [Bug Fixes](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-090-bug-fixes)
    
*   [Contributors](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#id5)
    

### Enhancements[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-090-enhancements "Permalink to this headline")

*   Added a timeout parameter to prevent infinite hangs ([GH790](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/790)
    )
    
*   Added AlphaVantage endpoint to get historical currency exchange rates ([GH764](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/764)
    )
    
*   Improved logging when rate limited ([GH745](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/745)
    )
    
*   Added daily historical data from Naver Finance ([GH722](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/722)
    )
    
*   Added the method `test` to the package to simplify running tests from an installation using
    

python -c "import pandas\_datareader; pandas\_datareader.test()"

### Backwards incompatible API changes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#backwards-incompatible-api-changes "Permalink to this headline")

*   Dropped support for Python 2.7. The minimum python version is now Python 3.6.
    
*   Removed Robinhood which no longer exists
    
*   Immediately deprecated AlphaVantage quote reader which used an end point that has been retired
    
*   Immediately deprecated Enigma which has substantially changed their business model and API
    
*   Immediately deprecated old symbol names for TSP to reflect the new website API
    

### Bug Fixes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-090-bug-fixes "Permalink to this headline")

*   Fix Yahoo Splits for change in format ([GH756](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/756)
    )
    
*   Fixed reading bond yields from Stooq ([GH752](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/752)
    )
    
*   Update TSP web scraper to new site ([GH740](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/740)
    )
    
*   Fixed EconDB reader to use session ([GH737](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/737)
    )
    
*   Fix reading futures data from Stooq ([GH718](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/718)
    )
    
*   Correct NASDAQ symbols fields link ([GH715](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/715)
    )
    
*   Fix Yahoo! actions bug due to change in split format ([GH755](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/755)
    )
    
*   Fix FutureWarning from pandas import ([GH762](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/762)
    )

v0.8.0 (September 22, 2019)[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#v0-8-0-september-22-2019 "Permalink to this headline")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Highlights include:

*   A new connector for Econdb was introduced. Econdb provides aggregated economic data from 90+ official statistical agencies ([GH615](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/615)
    )
    
*   Migrated IEX readers to [IEX Cloud](https://iexcloud.io/)
    . All readers now require an API token (`IEX_API_KEY`) ([GH638](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/638)
    )
    
*   Removal of Google Finance and Morningstar, which were deprecated in 0.7.0
    
*   Immediate deprecation of Robinhood for quotes and historical data. Robinhood ended support for these endpoints in 1/2019
    

What’s new in v0.8.0

*   [Enhancements](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-enhancements)
    
*   [Backwards incompatible API changes](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-api-breaking)
    
*   [Bug Fixes](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-bug-fixes)
    
*   [Contributors](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#id9)
    

### Enhancements[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-enhancements "Permalink to this headline")

*   Added Tiingo IEX Historical reader. ([GH619](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/619)
    )
    
*   Added support for Alpha Vantage intraday time series prices ([GH631](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/631)
    )
    
*   Up to 15 years of historical prices from IEX with new platform, IEX Cloud
    
*   Added testing on Python 3.7 ([GH667](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/667)
    )
    
*   Allow IEX to read less than 1 year of data ([GH649](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/649)
    )
    
*   Allow data download from Poland using stooq ([GH597](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/597)
    )
    
*   All time series readers now use a rolling default starting date (most are 5 years before the current date. Intraday readers are 3-5 days from the current date)
    

### Backwards incompatible API changes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-api-breaking "Permalink to this headline")

*   Immediate deprecation of Robinhood for quotes and historical data. Robinhood ended support for these endpoints in 1/2019. The Robinhood quotes and daily readers will raise an `ImmediateDeprecationError` when called.
    
*   Usage of all IEX readers requires an IEX Cloud API token, which can be passed as a parameter or stored in the environment variable `IEX_API_TOKEN`
    
*   Deprecated `access_key` in favor of `api_key` in `DataReader`. ([GH693](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/693)
    )
    

### Bug Fixes[¶](https://pandas-datareader.readthedocs.io/en/latest/whatsnew.html#whatsnew-080-bug-fixes "Permalink to this headline")

*   Fix Yahoo! actions issue where dividends are adjusted twice as a result of a change to the Yahoo! API. ([GH583](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/583)
    )
    
*   Fix AlphaVantage time series data ordering after provider switch to descending order (maintains ascending order for consistency). ([GH662](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/662)
    )
    
*   Refactored compatibility library to be independent of pandas version.
    
*   Fixed quarter value handling in JSDMX and OECD. ([GH685](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/685)
    )
    
*   Fixed a bug in `base` so that the reader does not error when response.encoding is `None`. ([GH674](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/674)
    )
    
*   Correct EcondbReader’s API URL format. ([GH670](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/670)
    )
    
*   Fix eurostat URL. ([GH669](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/669)
    )
    
*   Adjust Alphavantage time series reader to account for descending ordering. ([GH666](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/666)
    )
    
*   Fix bug in downloading index historical constituents. ([GH591](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/591)
    )
    
*   Fix a bug that occurs when an endpoint returns has no data for a date range. ([GH640](https://github.com/pydata/pandas-datareader/issues/640)
    )
